<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="kc1177_kraft_foods_inc._reports_2003___kra02826"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_kc1177_2"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=3><B>Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. Reports 2003 Results and<BR>  Announces Sustainable Growth Plan  <BR>  </B></FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Full-Year 2003 Diluted E.P.S. Up 2.6% To $2.01</I></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Fourth Quarter 2003 Diluted E.P.S. Down 7.4% To $0.50</I></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT
SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Full-Year Discretionary Cash Flow (Net Cash Provided By Operating Activities Less Capital Expenditures) Up 19.6% To $3.0
Billion</I></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Sustainable Growth Plan To Drive Brand Value, New Products And Global Scale</I></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Cost Restructuring Program
Expected To Cost Up To $1.2 Billion Pre-Tax Over Three Years</I></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Annual Pre-Tax Savings From Restructuring, Of Approximately $0.4 Billion By 2006, To Be Reinvested In
Marketing</I></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>2004 Diluted E.P.S. Guidance Of $1.63-$1.70, Including Approximately $0.30 In Charges From Restructuring Program</I></FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>NORTHFIELD,
IL&#151;January&nbsp;27, 2004&#151;Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. (NYSE: KFT) today reported full-year 2003 diluted earnings per share of $2.01, up 2.6% versus 2002,
and fourth quarter diluted earnings per share of $0.50, down 7.4% versus 2002. The company also outlined a new Sustainable Growth Plan to strengthen performance and achieve long-term
growth targets. The plan includes a cost restructuring program that is expected to result in pre-tax charges of up to $1.2&nbsp;billion over the next three years and generate
approximately $0.4&nbsp;billion in annual pre-tax savings by 2006. The company issued 2004 guidance, including diluted earnings per share of $1.63 to $1.70, which reflects a charge of
approximately $0.30 per share in total costs associated with the restructuring program. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"While
Kraft's fourth quarter results were in line with our expectations, we clearly are not satisfied with our performance in the quarter or for the full year," said Roger&nbsp;K.
Deromedi, Chief Executive Officer of Kraft Foods. "The corrective actions we began in late 2003 are showing progress, and the stronger steps we are announcing today will get us back on track for
sustainable growth." </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Deromedi
added, "We are committed to delivering consistent, long-term top and bottom line growth. Our Sustainable Growth Plan will reinvest the cost savings we generate to
build brand value, transform our portfolio and expand our global scale&#151;all supported by the new global 'One Company' organization structure we announced earlier this month." </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Deromedi
commented on the 2004 and longer-term outlook, saying, "While the charges associated with the restructuring program will lower our EPS in 2004, we are confident that
these actions will position Kraft to deliver sustainable EPS growth in the 6-9% range over the long-term." </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Fourth Quarter Results  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Diluted earnings per share declined 7.4% as lower operating income was partly offset by reduced interest expense and a lower effective tax rate. Operating income
declined 9.0% to $1,485&nbsp;million as higher commodity and benefit costs, the previously announced investment spending in focus categories, adverse product mix, and the absence of a prior year
gain on the sale of a business were partially offset by higher volume and by favorable currency of $46&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=1,EFW="2127259",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="2",CHK=223687,FOLIO='blank',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI7.04CHI1177]KC1177A.;16',USER='SLYUBOM',CD='27-JAN-2004;14:16' -->
<A NAME="page_kc1177_1_2"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
revenues increased 6.2% due to favorable currency of $303&nbsp;million, volume growth and pricing actions taken earlier in the year in response to commodity and devaluation-driven
cost increases, partially offset by unfavorable product mix, higher promotional spending and the impact of divestitures. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume
was up 1.1%, as volume growth from ongoing businesses of 1.9% was partially offset by the impact of divestitures. Tack-on acquisitions contributed 0.6 points of the
increase. Ongoing business volume was up in five of six segments, as consumption growth was partially offset by continued trade inventory reductions. A decline in the Biscuits, Snacks and
Confectionery segment was driven primarily by a decrease in biscuit volumes. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
the fourth quarter, the company invested $147&nbsp;million of a previously announced reinvestment program primarily in its U.S. focus categories. During the investment period,
cheese, cold cuts, coffee and crackers showed solid sequential improvement in consumption and share trends, while the cookie results remained weak. The previously cited factors impacting the cookie
category performance, including consumers' increased health and wellness focus and lower contributions from new products, continued to affect results in the fourth quarter. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During the quarter, the company declared a regular quarterly dividend of $0.18 per common share and repurchased 7.3&nbsp;million shares of Class&nbsp;A common
stock for $224&nbsp;million. The company also completed the sale of its Invernizzi cheese business in Italy, recording a net pre-tax gain on sale of $8&nbsp;million in the quarter. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Full-Year 2003 Results  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For the full-year, diluted earnings per share increased 2.6%, as lower financing costs, a lower effective tax rate and lower shares outstanding more
than offset a decline in operating income. Operating income declined 1.7% to $6,011&nbsp;million as higher commodity and benefit costs, unfavorable product mix and the impact of prior year gains on
the sales of businesses were partially offset by the absence of $253&nbsp;million in pre-tax integration-related and separation charges incurred in 2002, favorable currency of
$94&nbsp;million and volume growth. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
revenues increased 4.3%, due to favorable currency of $730&nbsp;million, volume growth and pricing actions, partially offset by higher promotional spending and the impact of
divestitures. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume
was up 0.7%, as volume growth from ongoing businesses of 1.6% was partially offset by the impact of divestitures. Ongoing volume growth reflected broad gains across reporting
segments and tack-on acquisitions, which accounted for 0.4&nbsp;points of growth, partially offset by a decline in the Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery segment and the impact of trade
inventory reductions. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>2</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=2,EFW="2127259",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="2",CHK=620671,FOLIO='2',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI7.04CHI1177]KC1177A.;16',USER='SLYUBOM',CD='27-JAN-2004;14:16' -->
<A NAME="page_kc1177_1_3"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Increased
focus on cash management drove a 19.6% increase in discretionary cash flow (net cash provided by operating activities less capital expenditures) to $3,034&nbsp;million,
through working capital changes, primarily inventory, higher net earnings and depreciation, and lower capital expenditures. Discretionary cash flow is available to finance acquisitions, repay maturing
debt, and distribute to shareholders. The company contributed $428&nbsp;million to its pension plans in 2003, an increase of $321&nbsp;million versus the prior year contributions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Sustainable Growth Plan  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The company is implementing a four-point Sustainable Growth Plan that is expected to deliver consistent, long-term growth in volume,
revenue and earnings. The plan's key elements are: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Significantly
higher investment in brand building through product innovation, more competitive pricing and world-class marketing;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Transformation
of the portfolio in-line with changing consumer and customer trends;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Expanded
global scale, particularly in the fastest-growing developing markets; and
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Reduced
cost structure with the reinvestment of savings into brand building initiatives. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
plan's fourth element includes a global restructuring program that will improve the company's cost structure and utilization of assets. Under this program, the company expects to
exit or close up to 20 of its production facilities worldwide and eliminate about 6,000 positions at all levels of the organization, or about 6% of its total workforce, over the next three years. The
company initially intends to close three plants in Canton, NY; Farmdale, OH; and Central Europe. Approximately 1,300 salaried positions in North America are expected to be eliminated in the first
quarter. The remaining reductions are expected to occur over the next three years. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
program is expected to cost up to $1.2&nbsp;billion pre-tax, with the majority of the charges to be incurred in 2004 and 2005. This estimated total includes
$1.1&nbsp;billion in pre-tax restructuring charges, primarily for asset write-offs and severance costs, and $0.1&nbsp;billion in associated pre-tax
implementation costs. Approximately half of the program's costs, or $0.6&nbsp;billion, are expected to be non-cash. Charges will be taken as programs are executed through 2006,
consistent with requirements under GAAP. In addition, the company expects to spend approximately $140&nbsp;million in capital over the next three years to implement the program. The program is
expected to generate approximately $0.4&nbsp;billion in annual pre-tax savings by 2006. In 2004, pre-tax charges under the restructuring program are estimated at
$750-$800&nbsp;million (approximately $0.30 per share), with
estimated pre-tax savings of $120-$140&nbsp;million ($0.05 per share) reinvested in brand building initiatives. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Outlook  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The company projects 2004 constant currency revenue growth of around 3% (including tack-on acquisitions and excluding the impact of divestitures),
supported by volume growth of 2-3%. Key volume growth drivers are higher marketing spending, new products, and developing market growth. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Diluted
earnings per share in 2004 is projected to be $1.63-$1.70, including the estimated $0.30 per share impact from charges associated with the restructuring program.
Other key items expected to impact earnings growth in 2004 include increased marketing and price management spending of $500-$600&nbsp;million ($0.19-$0.23 per share) on both
the U.S. focus categories and across the global portfolio, higher benefit costs ($0.05 per share), restricted stock expense ($0.02 per share), and gains on sales of businesses in 2003 ($0.01 per
share). Positive earnings drivers in 2004 are expected to include top-line growth and restructuring program savings. The factors described in the Forward-Looking and Cautionary Statements
section of this release represent continuing risks to these projections. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>3</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=3,EFW="2127259",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="2",CHK=477853,FOLIO='3',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI7.04CHI1177]KC1177A.;16',USER='SLYUBOM',CD='27-JAN-2004;14:16' -->
<A NAME="page_kc1177_1_4"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
company expects earnings to be skewed to the second half of the year, as top-line momentum builds during the year behind the increased marketing investment and the
majority of the restructuring program savings are not expected to be delivered until the second half. The first quarter in particular is expected to be down versus the prior year due to the magnitude
of the charges associated with the restructuring program and the increased marketing investment. The company expects first quarter EPS of $0.32-$0.35, including an estimated $0.10 per
share impact from charges associated with the restructuring program. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
a long-term basis, the Sustainable Growth Plan is expected to enable the company to deliver earnings per share growth of 6-9% excluding the impact of charges
associated with the restructuring program. Long-term revenue growth is expected to be around 3%, on volume growth of 2-3%, both including tack-on acquisitions. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>The company's fourth quarter and full-year 2003 results by segment are discussed under the reporting structure in place during 2003. As a result of
the organization changes announced on January&nbsp;8, 2004, the company will report financial results in a new segment structure beginning with the results for the first quarter of 2004 and will
provide restated historical results. The company will report six segments: US Beverages&nbsp;&amp; Grocery; US Snacks; US Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North American Foodservice; US Convenient
Meals; Europe Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The new segment structure in North America reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between segments to
align businesses with consumer targets. Results for the Mexico and Puerto Rico businesses, which were previously reported in the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, will be reported in the Latin
America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific segment.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>As described in "Note&nbsp;13, Segment Reporting" of Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc.'s 2002 Annual Report, management reviews operating companies income (OCI), which is
defined as operating income before corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. Management believes it is appropriate to disclose this
measure to help investors analyze business performance and trends. (For a reconciliation of OCI to operating income, see the Condensed Statements of Earnings contained in this
release.)</I></FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="kc1177_kraft_foods_north_america"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_kc1177_3"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>KRAFT FOODS NORTH AMERICA    <BR>    </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Fourth Quarter 2003 Results  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;OCI for Kraft Foods North America (KFNA) declined 8.0% to $1,088&nbsp;million, as increased commodity and benefit costs, unfavorable product mix and the
investment in focus categories were partially offset by the contribution from volume growth. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
revenues increased 2.9%, as volume growth, pricing actions taken earlier in the year in response to higher commodity costs, and favorable currency of $62&nbsp;million were
partially offset by increased promotional spending, particularly in the focus categories, to improve consumption and share trends. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume
grew 1.5%, led by contributions from new products and solid gains in Beverages, Cheese, Foodservice and Canada, partially offset by a decline in Biscuits and the impact of a
strike by grocery workers, particularly on the West Coast. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Following
are fourth quarter results by segment for KFNA: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Cheese, Meals and Enhancers</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume grew 2.7% behind strong gains in Cheese, Canada, and Foodservice. Net revenues increased 7.2%, as
volume growth and favorable currency of $62&nbsp;million were partially offset by higher promotional spending. The fourth quarter investment in Cheese had its intended effect, as all key cheese
segments recorded solid improvements in consumption and share trends. Growth in Canada was broad-based across the portfolio, while Foodservice volume increased due to growth in national accounts. OCI
increased 2.9% to $562&nbsp;million, as the impact of volume </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>4</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>

<A NAME="page_kc1177_1_5"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>growth,
pricing actions and favorable currency of $12&nbsp;million were partially offset by higher commodity and benefit costs and increased promotional spending. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume decreased 6.7%, driven primarily by cookies, reflecting the impact on the category of consumers'
increased health and wellness focus and fewer new product innovations than the prior year. Net revenues declined 6.2%, due to lower volume and increased promotional spending. In crackers, new </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>Ritz</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> Chips
continued to perform well. Confectionery volume declined, due to category softness and retail inventory reductions. OCI was down 34.7% to
$190&nbsp;million, as lower volume, increased promotional spending in biscuits and higher commodity costs were marginally offset by pricing actions and cost reduction efforts. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT

were also up 4.9%. New products including </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Capri Sun</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> Sport and </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Jell-O</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> Smoothies contributed
to growth in Beverages and Desserts. Coffee volume was down due to competitive activity, although both consumption and share trends showed improvement versus results earlier in the year. OCI was down
2.4% to $241&nbsp;million, as higher commodity and benefit costs and increased marketing spending were partially offset by volume growth and pricing actions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Oscar Mayer and Pizza</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume was up 1.4% and net revenues grew 3.2%. Cold cuts volume increased due to the investment to reduce price
gaps, and bacon and hot dog volumes were also up. Pizza volume was down slightly in a highly competitive environment. OCI declined 4.0% to $95&nbsp;million, as higher commodity and benefit costs and
unfavorable mix were partially offset by volume growth and pricing actions. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Full-Year 2003 Results  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;OCI for KFNA declined 0.7% to $4,920&nbsp;million, as higher commodity and benefit costs, unfavorable mix and increased promotional spending were partially
offset by the absence of $229&nbsp;million in pre-tax integration-related and separation charges incurred in 2002, volume growth and pricing actions taken early in the year in response
to higher commodity costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
revenues grew 2.0%, as higher volume, pricing actions and favorable currency of $120&nbsp;million were partially offset by increased second half promotional spending and adverse
mix. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume
was up 1.6%, due to contributions from new products and gains in Beverages, Foodservice, Canada, Mexico, and Cheese, partially offset by lower Biscuits volume and a reduction in
trade inventories. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Following
are full-year results by segment for KFNA: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Cheese, Meals and Enhancers</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume grew 1.7%, led by growth in Cheese, Foodservice, Canada, and Mexico. Net revenues increased 2.9%, due
to volume growth and favorable currency of $120&nbsp;million. Cheese volume was up due to improved consumption and share trends from the investment program that began in the third quarter.
Foodservice growth came from strength in national accounts, while solid performances from new products drove overall portfolio gains in Canada. In Mexico, strength in new </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>Clight</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> ready-to-drink beverages
contributed to growth. OCI increased 0.9% to $2,230&nbsp;million, reflecting
$90&nbsp;million in pre-tax integration-related and separation charges incurred in 2002, volume growth, pricing actions and favorable currency of $22&nbsp;million, partially offset by
higher commodity and benefit costs, increased promotional spending and adverse mix. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume declined 4.7%. Net revenues were down 1.8%, due to lower volume, higher promotional spending and
product returns, partially offset by favorable product mix. In Biscuits, cookie volume declined due to the impact of consumers' health and wellness focus, lower contributions from new products and
higher pricing, while cracker volume was down slightly with declines in </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Ritz</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> Bits partially offset by strength in </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Wheat
Thins</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Triscuit</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, and the introduction of </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Ritz</B></FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>5</FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Chips.

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="ke1177_kraft_foods_international"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_ke1177_1"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>KRAFT FOODS INTERNATIONAL    <BR>    </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Fourth Quarter 2003 Results  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;OCI for Kraft Foods International (KFI) decreased 7.7% to $442&nbsp;million, as the absence of a gain on sale of a business in 2002 and higher costs were
partially offset by pricing actions and favorable currency of $34&nbsp;million, reflecting the stronger Euro. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
revenues increased 13.2%, driven by favorable currency of $241&nbsp;million, pricing actions taken earlier in the year in response to higher commodity and devaluation-driven costs,
and volume growth, partially offset by the impact of divestitures. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume
was up 0.3%, as volume growth from ongoing businesses of 2.6% was offset by divestitures. Ongoing business volume was up due to tack-on acquisitions, which accounted
for 1.9 points of the increase, and growth in the Latin America and Asia Pacific segment. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Following
are fourth quarter results by segment for KFI: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Europe, Middle East and Africa (EMEA)</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume was up 0.1%, as gains from acquisitions and solid growth in the United Kingdom, Poland and
Russia were offset by a 0.8&nbsp;percentage point impact from divestitures as well as price competition, particularly in Germany, France and Ukraine. Net revenues were up 11.7%, due primarily to
favorable currency of $205&nbsp;million. OCI increased 1.8% to $346&nbsp;million, driven by favorable currency of $30&nbsp;million and a pre-tax gain on sale of the Invernizzi cheese
business of $8&nbsp;million, partially offset by higher costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Latin America and Asia Pacific (LAAP)</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume increased 0.7%. Ongoing business volume was up 5.1%, due to solid growth in numerous markets
including Argentina, Brazil and China. Net revenues were up 18.8%, driven by pricing actions in response to devaluation-driven cost increases, currency favorability
of $36&nbsp;million and volume growth. OCI was down 30.9% to $96&nbsp;million, reflecting the absence of a $69&nbsp;million pre-tax gain on sale of a business in 2002, partially
offset by volume growth and pricing actions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Full-Year 2003 Results  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;OCI for KFI decreased 3.6% to $1,282&nbsp;million, as the absence of gains on sales of businesses in 2002, unfavorable mix, higher benefit costs and
infrastructure investment in developing markets were partially offset by the absence of $24&nbsp;million in pre-tax integration-related and separation charges incurred in 2002, pricing
actions, and favorable currency of $72&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
revenues grew 10.5% to $9,103&nbsp;million, as favorable currency of $610&nbsp;million&#151;benefiting from the strength of the Euro&#151;and pricing actions to
offset higher commodity and Latin American devaluation-driven cost increases were partially offset by divestitures. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume
decreased 1.6%, as the impact of divestitures more than offset volume growth from ongoing businesses of 1.4%. Ongoing business volume was up due to tack-on
acquisitions, which accounted for 1.5 points of growth, and growth in several key developing markets including Russia, Brazil, and China, moderated by the impact of price competition, particularly in
Germany and France, and the impact of the summer heat wave in Europe on the coffee and confectionery businesses. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Following
are full-year results by segment for KFI: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Europe, Middle East and Africa (EMEA)</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume increased 0.3%, as ongoing volume growth of 0.8% was partially offset by the impact of
divestitures. Volume growth was driven by acquisitions and by gains in Italy, the United Kingdom, Poland and Russia, partially offset by the impact of price competition in Germany and France. Net
revenues increased 13.6%, driven by favorable currency of $808&nbsp;million, pricing actions and volume growth. OCI increased 5.2% to $1,012&nbsp;million, driven by favorable currency of
$100&nbsp;million and pre-tax gains on the sales of businesses in 2003 of $31&nbsp;million, </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>7</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=7,EFW="2127259",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="2",CHK=256859,FOLIO='7',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI7.04CHI1177]KE1177A.;7',USER='SLYUBOM',CD='27-JAN-2004;14:16' -->
<A NAME="page_ke1177_1_8"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>partially
offset by unfavorable mix, lower margins, higher benefit costs and infrastructure investments in Eastern Europe. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;EMEA
coffee volume was down, reflecting the impacts of price competition and the summer heat wave in Europe. However, volume was up strongly in Russia, benefiting from expanded
distribution of </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>Maxwell House</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> and </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Jacobs</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> coffees, and in Poland due to the launch of </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Jacobs Ice
Presso</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> ready-to-drink coffee and </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Maxwell House</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> 3-in-1. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;EMEA
snacks volume was up, as an increase in biscuits and salted snacks due to acquisitions was partially offset by a decline in confectionery due to the impacts of price competition and
the summer heat wave. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;EMEA
cheese volume was down, as lower volume in Spain and Germany due to price competition was moderated by growth in Italy, benefiting from new products and marketing programs
supporting </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Philadelphia</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> cream cheese. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;EMEA
convenient meals volume was lower, as growth in </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Simmenthal</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> canned meats in Italy was more than offset by the divestiture of the </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>reis-fit</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> business in
Europe. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Latin America and Asia Pacific (LAAP)</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume decreased 4.4%, due to the impact of divestitures. Volume from ongoing businesses was up
2.3%, driven by gains in key markets including Argentina, Brazil, China and Australia. Net revenues increased 1.1%, as higher pricing and ongoing volume growth was partially offset by unfavorable
currency of $198&nbsp;million, the impact of a divestiture and unfavorable mix. OCI decreased 26.6% to $270&nbsp;million, as $72&nbsp;million in pre-tax gains on sales of businesses
in 2002, adverse currency of $28&nbsp;million, and higher costs were partially offset by pricing to cover devaluation-driven cost increases and the absence of $19&nbsp;million in
pre-tax integration-related and separation charges incurred in 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LAAP
snacks volume grew, as gains in biscuits in Brazil, Argentina, China and Australia driven by new products, were partially offset by a decline in confectionery, which was impacted by
economic weakness, trade inventory reductions and price competition in Brazil. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LAAP
beverages volume grew strongly, driven by double-digit gains in Brazil, Venezuela and China, benefiting from new products. Grocery volume was lower, reflecting the divestiture of
the bakery ingredients business in 2002. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>*&nbsp;&nbsp;*&nbsp;&nbsp;*
</FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
company will present its 2003 results, 2004 outlook and plan for delivering sustainable growth to members of the investment community and media at 4:30&nbsp;p.m. ET on
January&nbsp;27, 2004, in New York.
Access to a live audio webcast of the presentation, including the presentation slides, is available at </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>www.kraft.com</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>. A replay of the presentation will
be available on the company's web site. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Kraft
Foods&nbsp;Inc. is the largest branded food and beverage company headquartered in the United States and the second largest worldwide. Kraft Foods markets many of the world's
leading food brands, including </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Kraft</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> cheese, </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Jacobs</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> and </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Maxwell
House</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> coffees, </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Nabisco</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> cookies and crackers, </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Philadelphia</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> cream cheese, </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>Oscar Mayer</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>
meats, </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Post</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> cereals and </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Milka</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> chocolates, in
more than 150 countries. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Company is subject to unfavorable currency movements, intense competition, changes in consumer preferences and demand for its products, including publicity concerning the health
implications of obesity and trans fatty acids, changing prices for raw materials, fluctuations in levels of customer inventories and the effects of foreign economies and local economic and market
conditions. The Company's benefit expense is subject to the investment performance of pension plan assets, interest rates and cost increases for medical benefits offered to employees and retirees. The
Company's results are dependent upon its continued ability to promote brand equity successfully; to anticipate and respond to new consumer trends; to develop new products and markets and to broaden
brand portfolios; to compete effectively with lower-priced products in a consolidating environment at the retail and manufacturing levels; to improve productivity; to realize the cost savings and
improved asset utilization contemplated by its restructuring program; to consummate and successfully integrate acquisitions; and other risks detailed from time to time in the Company's publicly filed
documents. The Company's results are also dependent upon its access to credit markets, its borrowing costs and its credit ratings, which may in turn be influenced by the credit ratings of Altria
Group,&nbsp;Inc. The Company cautions that the foregoing list of important factors is not exclusive, any forward-looking statement included in this press release is made as of the date of this press
